258→\n   259→void ConnectionManagerImpl::doEndStream(ActiveStream& stream, bool check_for_deferred_close) {\n   260→  // The order of what happens in this routine is important and a little complicated. We first see\n   261→  // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\n   262→  // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\n   263→  // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. This\n   264→  // must be done after deleting the stream since the stream refers to the connection and must be\n   265→  // deleted first.\n   266→  bool reset_stream = false;\n   267→  // If the response encoder is still associated with the stream, reset the stream. The most significant gaps involve connection-level lifecycle management (idle timeouts, duration limits), premature stream reset detection, and protocol-specific error handling paths. These gaps could allow bugs in connection draining logic, resource cleanup, and edge-case protocol violations to slip through without detection.\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Connection Idle Timeout Without Codec Creation\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~759-763\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: The `onIdleTimeout()` function has a code path that executes when the connection becomes idle before any HTTP codec is created (e.g., TLS handshake timeout or slow client). This path calls `doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWrite)` differently than the codec-present path. This edge case is untested.\n- **Proposed Test**: `ConnectionIdleTimeoutWithoutCodec`\n  - Set up connection manager with idle timeout configured\n  - Do NOT trigger codec creation (don't send any data)\n  - Wait for idle timer to fire via mock timer\n  - Verify `downstream_cx_idle_timeout_` stat incremented\n  - Verify `doConnectionClose()` called with FlushWrite close type\n  - Verify no codec protocol stats modified\n- **Why It Matters**: Connection cleanup without codec could leak resources or fail to flush pending data. If this code path is broken, idle connections that never complete protocol negotiation might not close properly, exhausting connection limits.\n\n### Gap 2: HTTP/1 Safe Max Connection Duration (Soft Drain)\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~778-783\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: When `onConnectionDurationTimeout()` fires on an HTTP/1 connection with `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` configured, the code enters a special \"soft drain\" mode by setting `soft_drain_http1_ = true`. If untested, the feature could fail silently, allowing smuggling attacks or leaving connections in inconsistent states.\n\n### Gap 3: Premature Stream Reset Detection and Automatic Drain\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~702-748 (maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets) and ~677-698 (isPrematureRstStream)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: The connection manager tracks streams that close prematurely (reset without sending response). When the count exceeds runtime-configurable thresholds, it automatically drains the connection via GOAWAY. This is security-critical for detecting attacks, but the logic is completely untested. The function uses complex threshold calculations (lines 724-738) that must behave correctly.\n- **Proposed Test**: `MaybeDrainDueToPrematureResetsTriggersGoaway`\n  - Configure `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` runtime value to 5\n  - Configure `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds` to 0 (any stream < 1 sec is premature)\n  - Create 6 streams, each with no response sent before reset\n  - After 6th stream reset, verify:\n    - `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag is set\n    - `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat incremented\n    - `doConnectionClose()` called with Abort close type\n    - No further resets are checked (guard against recursion)\n  - Also test: threshold math where 50% of streams are premature (line 731, 735 conditions)\n- **Why It Matters**: Premature resets can indicate slowloris attacks or protocol violations. Untested code could fail to detect attacks or trigger false positives. The recursive protection (line 716-717) is untested and could fail, causing stack overflow.\n\n### Gap 4: HTTP/2 Codec GoAway Frame Reception\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~751-754\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: The `onGoAway()` callback is invoked when the remote peer sends an HTTP/2 GOAWAY frame.
